HARRY and the Sorcerer's Stone
CHAPTER ONE
THE BOY WHO LIVED
Mr. and PETUNIA , of number four, Privet Drive, were proud to say that they were perfectly normal, thank you very much. 
They were the last people you'd expect to be involved in anything strange or mysterious, because they just didn't hold with such nonsense.
VERNON was the director of a firm called Grunnings, which made drills. 
VERNON was a big, beefy man with hardly any neck, although VERNON did have a very large mustache. 
PETUNIA was thin and blonde and had nearly twice the usual amount of neck, which came in very useful as PETUNIA spent so much of PETUNIA's time craning over garden fences, spying on the neighbors. 
The DURSLEYS had a small son called DUDLEY and in their opinion there was no finer boy anywhere.
The DURSLEYS had everything they wanted, but they also had a secret, and their greatest fear was that somebody would discover it. 
They didn't think they could bear it if anyone found out about the POTTERS. 
LILY was PETUNIA 's sister, but they hadn't met for several years; in fact, PETUNIA pretended PETUNIA didn't have a sister, because PETUNIA's sister and PETUNIA's good-for-nothing husband were as unDursleyish as it was possible to be. 
The DURSLEYS shuddered to think what the neighbors would say if the POTTERS arrived in the street. 
The DURSLEYS knew that the POTTERS had a small son, too, but they had never even seen him. 
This boy was another good reason for keeping the POTTERS away; they didn't want DUDLEY mixing with a child like that.
When Mr. and PETUNIA woke up on the dull, gray Tuesday our story starts, there was nothing about the cloudy sky outside to suggest that strange and mysterious things would soon be happening all over the country. 
VERNON hummed as VERNON picked out VERNON's most boring tie for work, and PETUNIA gossiped away happily as PETUNIA wrestled a screaming DUDLEY into DUDLEY's high chair.
None of them noticed a large, tawny owl flutter past the window.
At half past eight, VERNON picked up VERNON's briefcase, pecked PETUNIA on the cheek, and tried to kiss DUDLEY good-bye but missed, because DUDLEY was now having a tantrum and throwing DUDLEY's cereal at the walls. 
###DIALOGUE###``Little tyke,'' chortled VERNON as VERNON left the house. 
VERNON got into VERNON's car and backed out of number four's drive.
It was on the corner of the street that VERNON noticed the first sign of something peculiar -- a cat reading a map. 
For a second, VERNON didn't realize what VERNON had seen -- then VERNON jerked VERNON's head around to look again. 
There was a tabby cat standing on the corner of Privet Drive, but there wasn't a map in sight. 
What could VERNON have been thinking of? 
It must have been a trick of the light. 
VERNON blinked and stared at the cat. 
It stared back. 
As VERNON drove around the corner and up the road, VERNON watched the cat in VERNON's mirror. 
It was now reading the sign that said Privet Drive -- no, looking at the sign; cats couldn't read maps or signs. 
VERNON gave himself a little shake and put the cat out of VERNON's mind. 
As VERNON drove toward town VERNON thought of nothing except a large order of drills VERNON was hoping to get that day.
But on the edge of town, drills were driven out of VERNON's mind by something else. 
As VERNON sat in the usual morning traffic jam, VERNON couldn't help noticing that there seemed to be a lot of strangely dressed people about. 
People in cloaks. 
VERNON couldn't bear people who dressed in funny clothes -- the getups you saw on young people! 
VERNON supposed this was some stupid new fashion. 
VERNON drummed VERNON's fingers on the steering wheel and VERNON's eyes fell on a huddle of these weirdos standing quite close by. 
They were whispering excitedly together. 
VERNON was enraged to see that a couple of them weren't young at all; why, that man had to be older than VERNON was, and wearing an emerald-green cloak! 
The nerve of VERNON! 
But then it struck VERNON that this was probably some silly stunt -- these people were obviously collecting for something...
yes, that would be it. 
The traffic moved on and a few minutes later, VERNON arrived in the Grunnings parking lot, VERNON's mind back on drills.
VERNON always sat with VERNON's back to the window in VERNON's office on the ninth floor. 
If VERNON hadn't, VERNON might have found it harder to concentrate on drills that morning. 
VERNON didn't see the owls swoop ing past in broad daylight, though people down in the street did; they pointed and gazed open- mouthed as owl after owl sped overhead. 
Most of them had never seen an owl even at nighttime. 
VERNON , however, had a perfectly normal, owl-free morning. 
VERNON yelled at five different people. 
VERNON made several important telephone calls and shouted a bit more. 
VERNON was in a very good mood until lunchtime, when VERNON thought VERNON'd stretch VERNON's legs and walk across the road to buy himself a bun from the bakery.
VERNON'd forgotten all about the people in cloaks until VERNON passed a group of them next to the baker's. 
VERNON eyed them angrily as VERNON passed. 
VERNON didn't know why, but they made VERNON uneasy. 
This bunch were whispering excitedly, too, and VERNON couldn't see a single collecting tin. 
It was on VERNON's way back past them, clutching a large doughnut in a bag, that VERNON caught a few words of what they were saying.
###DIALOGUE###``The POTTERS, that's right, that's what I heard yes, their son, HARRY''
VERNON stopped dead. 
Fear flooded VERNON. 
VERNON looked back at the whisperers as if VERNON wanted to say something to them, but thought better of it.
VERNON dashed back across the road, hurried up to VERNON's office, snapped at VERNON's secretary not to disturb VERNON, seized VERNON's telephone, and had almost finished dialing VERNON's home number when VERNON changed VERNON's mind. 
VERNON put the receiver back down and stroked VERNON's mustache, thinking... no, VERNON was being stupid. 
HARRY wasn't such an unusual name. 
HARRY was sure there were lots of people called HARRY who had a son called HARRY. 
Come to think of it, HARRY wasn't even sure HARRY's nephew was called HARRY. 
HARRY'd never even seen the boy. 
It might have been Harvey. 
Or Harold. 
There was no point in worrying PETUNIA ; PETUNIA always got so upset at any mention of PETUNIA's sister. 
He didn't blame PETUNIA's -- if he'd had a sister like that... but all the same, those people in cloaks...
He found it a lot harder to concentrate on drills that afternoon and when he left the building at five o'clock, he was still so worried that he walked straight into someone just outside the door.
###DIALOGUE###``Sorry,'' he grunted, as the tiny old man stumbled and almost fell. 
It was a few seconds before VERNON realized that the man was wearing a violet cloak. 
VERNON didn't seem at all upset at being almost knocked to the ground. 
###DIALOGUE###On the contrary, VERNON's face split into a wide smile and VERNON said in a squeaky voice that made passersby stare, ``Don't be sorry, my dear sir, for nothing could upset me today! 
###DIALOGUE###Rejoice, for YOU-KNOW-WHO has gone at last! 
###DIALOGUE###Even Muggles like yourself should be celebrating, this happy, happy day!''
And the old man hugged VERNON around the middle and walked off.
VERNON stood rooted to the spot. 
VERNON had been hugged by a complete stranger. 
VERNON also thought VERNON had been called a Muggle, whatever that was. 
VERNON was rattled. 
VERNON hurried to VERNON's car and set off for home, hoping VERNON was imagining things, which VERNON had never hoped before, because VERNON didn't approve of imagination.
As VERNON pulled into the driveway of number four, the first thing VERNON saw -- and it didn't improve VERNON's mood -- was the tabby cat VERNON'd spotted that morning. 
It was now sitting on VERNON's garden wall. 
VERNON was sure it was the same one; it had the same markings around its eyes.
###DIALOGUE###``Shoo!'' said VERNON loudly. 
The cat didn't move. 
It just gave VERNON a stern look. 
Was this normal cat behavior? 
VERNON wondered. 
Trying to pull himself together, VERNON let himself into the house. 
VERNON was still determined not to mention anything to VERNON's wife.
PETUNIA had had a nice, normal day. 
PETUNIA told VERNON over dinner all about Mrs. Next Door's problems with PETUNIA's daughter and how DUDLEY had learned a new word -LRB-``Won't!''-RRB-
. 
VERNON tried to act normally. 
###DIALOGUE###When DUDLEY had been put to bed, VERNON went into the living room in time to catch the last report on the evening news: ``And finally, bird-watchers everywhere have reported that the nation's owls have been behaving very unusually today. 
###DIALOGUE###Although owls normally hunt at night and are hardly ever seen in daylight, there have been hundreds of sightings of these birds flying in every direction since sunrise. 
###DIALOGUE###Experts are unable to explain why the owls have suddenly changed their sleeping pattern.'' 
The newscaster allowed himself a grin.
###DIALOGUE###``Most mysterious. 
###DIALOGUE###And now, over to Jim McGuffin with the weather. 
###DIALOGUE###Going to be any more showers of owls tonight, Jim?''
###DIALOGUE###``Well, Ted,'' said the weatherman, ``I don't know about that, but it's not only the owls that have been acting oddly today. 
###DIALOGUE###Viewers as far apart as Kent, Yorkshire, and Dundee have been phoning in to tell me that instead of the rain I promised yesterday, they've had a downpour of shooting stars! 
###DIALOGUE###Perhaps people have been celebrating Bonfire Night early -- it's not until next week, folks! 
###DIALOGUE###But I can promise a wet night tonight.''
VERNON sat frozen in VERNON's armchair. 
Shooting stars all over Britain? 
Owls flying by daylight? 
Mysterious people in cloaks all over the place? 
And a whisper, a whisper about the POTTERS...
PETUNIA came into the living room carrying two cups of tea. 
It was no good. 
VERNON'd have to say something to PETUNIA. 
VERNON cleared VERNON's throat nervously. 
###DIALOGUE###``Er -- PETUNIA, dear -- you haven't heard from your sister lately, have you?''
As VERNON had expected, PETUNIA looked shocked and angry. 
After all, they normally pretended PETUNIA didn't have a sister.
###DIALOGUE###``No,'' PETUNIA said sharply. 
###DIALOGUE###``Why?''
###DIALOGUE###``Funny stuff on the news,'' VERNON mumbled. 
###DIALOGUE###``Owls... shooting stars... and there were a lot of funny-looking people in town today...''
###DIALOGUE###``So?'' snapped PETUNIA .
###DIALOGUE###``Well, I just thought... maybe... it was something to do with... you know... her crowd.''
PETUNIA sipped PETUNIA's tea through pursed lips. 
###DIALOGUE###VERNON wondered whether VERNON dared tell PETUNIA VERNON'd heard the name ``HARRY.'' 
VERNON decided VERNON didn't dare. 
###DIALOGUE###Instead VERNON said, as casually as VERNON could, ``Their son -- HARRY'd be about DUDLEY's age now, wouldn't HARRY?''
###DIALOGUE###``I suppose so,'' said PETUNIA stiffly.
###DIALOGUE###``What's HARRY's name again? 
###DIALOGUE###Howard, isn't it?''
###DIALOGUE###``HARRY. 
###DIALOGUE###Nasty, common name, if you ask me.''
###DIALOGUE###``Oh, yes,'' said VERNON , VERNON's heart sinking horribly. 
###DIALOGUE###``Yes, I quite agree.''
VERNON didn't say another word on the subject as they went upstairs to bed.
While PETUNIA was in the bathroom, VERNON crept to the bedroom window and peered down into the front garden. 
The cat was still there.
It was staring down Privet Drive as though it were waiting for something.
Was VERNON imagining things? 
Could all this have anything to do with the POTTERS? 
If it did... if it got out that they were related to a pair of -- well, VERNON didn't think VERNON could bear it.
The Dursleys got into bed. 
PETUNIA fell asleep quickly but VERNON lay awake, turning it all over in VERNON's mind. 
VERNON's last, comforting thought before VERNON fell asleep was that even if the POTTERS were involved, there was no reason for them to come near VERNON and PETUNIA . 
The POTTERS knew very well what VERNON and PETUNIA thought about them and their kind... VERNON couldn't see how VERNON and PETUNIA could get mixed up in anything that might be going on -- VERNON yawned and turned over -- it couldn't affect them...
How very wrong VERNON was.
VERNON might have been drifting into an uneasy sleep, but the cat on the wall outside was showing no sign of sleepiness. 
It was sitting as still as a statue, its eyes fixed unblinkingly on the far corner of Privet Drive. 
It didn't so much as quiver when a car door slammed on the next street, nor when two owls swooped overhead. 
In fact, it was nearly midnight before the cat moved at all.
A man appeared on the corner the cat had been watching, appeared so suddenly and silently you'd have thought he'd just popped out of the ground. 
The cat's tail twitched and its eyes narrowed.
Nothing like this man had ever been seen on Privet Drive. 
He was tall, thin, and very old, judging by the silver of his hair and beard, which were both long enough to tuck into his belt. 
He was wearing long robes, a purple cloak that swept the ground, and high-heeled, buckled boots.
His blue eyes were light, bright, and sparkling behind half-moon spectacles and his nose was very long and crooked, as though it had been broken at least twice. 
This man's name was DUMBLEDORE .
DUMBLEDORE didn't seem to realize that DUMBLEDORE had just arrived in a street where everything from DUMBLEDORE's name to DUMBLEDORE's boots was unwelcome. 
DUMBLEDORE was busy rummaging in DUMBLEDORE's cloak, looking for something. 
But DUMBLEDORE did seem to realize DUMBLEDORE was being watched, because DUMBLEDORE looked up suddenly at the cat, which was still staring at DUMBLEDORE from the other end of the street. 
For some reason, the sight of the cat seemed to amuse DUMBLEDORE. 
###DIALOGUE###DUMBLEDORE chuckled and muttered, ``I should have known.''
DUMBLEDORE found what DUMBLEDORE was looking for in DUMBLEDORE's inside pocket. 
It seemed to be a silver cigarette lighter. 
DUMBLEDORE flicked it open, held it up in the air, and clicked it. 
The nearest street lamp went out with a little pop. 
DUMBLEDORE clicked it again -- the next lamp flickered into darkness. 
Twelve times DUMBLEDORE clicked the Put-Outer, until the only lights left on the whole street were two tiny pinpricks in the distance, which were the eyes of the cat watching DUMBLEDORE. 
If anyone looked out of their window now, even beady-eyed PETUNIA , they wouldn't be able to see anything that was happening down on the pavement. 
DUMBLEDORE slipped the Put-Outer back inside DUMBLEDORE's cloak and set off down the street toward number four, where DUMBLEDORE sat down on the wall next to the cat. 
DUMBLEDORE didn't look at it, but after a moment DUMBLEDORE spoke to it.
###DIALOGUE###``Fancy seeing you here, MCGONAGALL.''
DUMBLEDORE turned to smile at the tabby, but it had gone. 
Instead DUMBLEDORE was smiling at a rather severe-looking woman who was wearing square glasses exactly the shape of the markings the cat had had around its eyes. 
MCGONAGALL, too, was wearing a cloak, an emerald one. 
MCGONAGALL's black hair was drawn into a tight bun. 
MCGONAGALL looked distinctly ruffled.
###DIALOGUE###``How did you know it was me?'' MCGONAGALL asked.
###DIALOGUE###``My dear Professor, I 've never seen a cat sit so stiffly.''
###DIALOGUE###``You'd be stiff if you'd been sitting on a brick wall all day,'' said MCGONAGALL.
###DIALOGUE###``All day? 
###DIALOGUE###When you could have been celebrating? 
###DIALOGUE###I must have passed a dozen feasts and parties on my way here.'' 
MCGONAGALL sniffed angrily.
###DIALOGUE###``Oh yes, everyone's celebrating, all right,'' she said impatiently.
###DIALOGUE###``You'd think they'd be a bit more careful, but no -- even the Muggles have noticed something's going on. 
###DIALOGUE###It was on their news.'' 
She jerked her head back at the DURSLEYS' dark living-room window. 
###DIALOGUE###``I heard it. 
###DIALOGUE###Flocks of owls... shooting stars... Well, they're not completely stupid. 
###DIALOGUE###They were bound to notice something. 
###DIALOGUE###Shooting stars down in Kent -- I'll bet that was DIGGLE. 
###DIALOGUE###DIGGLE never had much sense.''
###DIALOGUE###``You can't blame them,'' said DUMBLEDORE gently. 
###DIALOGUE###``We've had precious little to celebrate for eleven years.''
###DIALOGUE###``I know that,'' said MCGONAGALL irritably. 
###DIALOGUE###``But that's no reason to lose our heads. 
###DIALOGUE###People are being downright careless, out on the streets in broad daylight, not even dressed in Muggle clothes, swapping rumors.''
MCGONAGALL threw a sharp, sideways glance at DUMBLEDORE here, as though hoping DUMBLEDORE was going to tell her something, but DUMBLEDORE didn't, so she went on. 
###DIALOGUE###``A fine thing it would be if, on the very day YOU-KNOW-WHO seems to have disappeared at last, the Muggles found out about us all. 
###DIALOGUE###I suppose he really has gone, DUMBLEDORE?''
###DIALOGUE###``It certainly seems so,'' said DUMBLEDORE. 
###DIALOGUE###``We have much to be thankful for. 
###DIALOGUE###Would you care for a lemon drop?''
###DIALOGUE###``A what?''
###DIALOGUE###``A lemon drop. 
###DIALOGUE###They're a kind of Muggle sweet I'm rather fond of''
###DIALOGUE###``No, thank you,'' said MCGONAGALL coldly, as though she didn't think this was the moment for lemon drops. 
###DIALOGUE###``As I say, even if YOU-KNOW-WHO has gone -''
###DIALOGUE###``My dear Professor, surely a sensible person like yourself can call him by his name? 
###DIALOGUE###All this `YOU-KNOW-WHO' nonsense -- for eleven years I have been trying to persuade people to call him by his proper name: VOLDEMORT.'' 
MCGONAGALL flinched, but DUMBLEDORE, who was unsticking two lemon drops, seemed not to notice. 
###DIALOGUE###``It all gets so confusing if we keep saying `YOU-KNOW-WHO.' 
###DIALOGUE###I have never seen any reason to be frightened of saying VOLDEMORT's name.
###DIALOGUE###``I know you haven `t, said MCGONAGALL, sounding half exasperated, half admiring. 
###DIALOGUE###``But you're different. 
###DIALOGUE###Everyone knows you're the only one You-Know- oh, all right, VOLDEMORT, was frightened of.''
###DIALOGUE###``You flatter me,'' said DUMBLEDORE calmly. 
###DIALOGUE###``VOLDEMORT had powers I will never have.''
###DIALOGUE###``Only because you're too -- well -- noble to use them.''
###DIALOGUE###``It's lucky it's dark. 
###DIALOGUE###I haven't blushed so much since POMFREY told me POMFREY liked my new earmuffs.''

###DIALOGUE###You know what everyone's saying? 
###DIALOGUE###About why VOLDEMORT's disappeared? 
###DIALOGUE###About what finally stopped VOLDEMORT?''
It seemed that MCGONAGALL had reached the point MCGONAGALL was most anxious to discuss, the real reason MCGONAGALL had been waiting on a cold, hard wall all day, for neither as a cat nor as a woman had she fixed DUMBLEDORE with such a piercing stare as MCGONAGALL did now. 
It was plain that whatever ``everyone'' was saying, MCGONAGALL was not going to believe it until DUMBLEDORE told MCGONAGALL it was true. 
DUMBLEDORE, however, was choosing another lemon drop and did not answer.
###DIALOGUE###``What they're saying,'' MCGONAGALL pressed on, ``is that last night VOLDEMORT turned up in Godric's Hollow. 
###DIALOGUE###VOLDEMORT went to find the POTTERS. 
###DIALOGUE###The rumor is that LILY and JAMES are -- are -- that they're -- dead.
###DIALOGUE###DUMBLEDORE bowed DUMBLEDORE's head.

###DIALOGUE###``LILY and JAMES... I can't believe it... I didn't want to believe it...
###DIALOGUE###Oh, DUMBLEDORE...''

###DIALOGUE###``I know... I know...'' DUMBLEDORE said heavily.

###DIALOGUE###``That's not all.

VOLDEMORT couldn't kill that little boy.

A low rumbling sound had broken the silence around them. 
It grew steadily louder as they looked up and down the street for some sign of a headlight; it swelled to a roar as they both looked up at the sky -- and a huge motorcycle fell out of the air and landed on the road in front of them.
If the motorcycle was huge, it was nothing to the man sitting astride it. 
HAGRID was almost twice as tall as a normal man and at least five times as wide. 
HAGRID looked simply too big to be allowed, and so wild - long tangles of bushy black hair and beard hid most of his face, HAGRID had hands the size of trash can lids, and HAGRID's feet in their leather boots were like baby dolphins.

###DIALOGUE###I've got him, sir.''

###DIALOGUE###``Shhh!''

CHAPTER FIVE
DIAGON ALLEY

CHAPTER SIX
THE JOURNEY FROM PLATFORM NINE AND THREE-QUARTERS
HARRY's last month with the DURSLEYS wasn't fun.

CHAPTER SEVEN
THE SORTING HAT
The door swung open at once. 
A tall, black-haired witch in emerald-green robes stood there. 
She had a very stern face and HARRY's first thought was that this was not someone to cross.
###DIALOGUE###``The firs' years, MCGONAGALL,'' said HAGRID.
###DIALOGUE###``Thank you, HAGRID. 
###DIALOGUE###I will take them from here.''
She pulled the door wide. 
The entrance hall was so big you could have fit the whole of the DURSLEYS' house in it. 
The stone walls were lit with flaming torches like the ones at GRINGOTTS, the ceiling was too high to make out, and a magnificent marble staircase facing them led to the upper floors.
They followed MCGONAGALL across the flagged stone floor. 
HARRY could hear the dRONe of hundreds of voices from a doorway to the right -the rest of the school must already be here -- but MCGONAGALL showed the first years into a small, empty chamber off the hall. 
They crowded in, standing rather closer together than they would usually have done, peering about nervously.
###DIALOGUE###``Welcome to HOGWARTS,'' said MCGONAGALL. 
###DIALOGUE###``The start-of-term banquet will begin shortly, but before you take your seats in the Great Hall, you will be sorted into your houses. 
###DIALOGUE###The Sorting is a very important ceremony because, while you are here, your house will be something like your family within HOGWARTS. 
###DIALOGUE###You will have classes with the rest of your house, sleep in your house dormitory, and spend free time in your house common room.
###DIALOGUE###``The four houses are called GRYFFINDOR, HUFFLEPUFF, RAVENCLAW, and SLYTHERIN. 
###DIALOGUE###Each house has its own noble history and each has produced outstanding witches and wizards. 
###DIALOGUE###While you are at HOGWARTS, your triumphs will earn your house points, while any rulebreaking will lose house points. 
###DIALOGUE###At the end of the year, the house with the most points is awarded the house cup, a great honor. 
###DIALOGUE###I hope each of you will be a credit to whichever house becomes yours.
###DIALOGUE###``The Sorting Ceremony will take place in a few minutes in front of the rest of the school. 
###DIALOGUE###I suggest you all smarten yourselves up as much as you can while you are waiting.''
Her eyes lingered for a moment on NEVILLE's cloak, which was fastened under NEVILLE's left ear, and on RON's smudged nose. 
HARRY nervously tried to flatten HARRY's hair.
###DIALOGUE###``I shall return when we are ready for you,'' said MCGONAGALL.
###DIALOGUE###``Please wait quietly.''
She left the chamber.

CHAPTER EIGHT
THE POTIONS MASTER
###DIALOGUE###There, look.''
###DIALOGUE###``Where?''
###DIALOGUE###``Next to the tall kid with the red hair.''
###DIALOGUE###``Wearing the glasses?''
###DIALOGUE###``Did you see his face?''
###DIALOGUE###``Did you see his scar?''
Whispers followed HARRY from the moment HARRY left HARRY's dormitory the next day. 
People lining up outside classrooms stood on tiptoe to get a look at HARRY, or doubled back to pass HARRY in the corridors again, staring.
HARRY wished they wouldn't, because HARRY was trying to concentrate on finding HARRY's way to classes.
There were a hundred and forty-two staircases at HOGWARTS: wide, sweeping ones; narrow, rickety ones; some that led somewhere different on a Friday; some with a vanishing step halfway up that you had to remember to jump. 
Then there were doors that wouldn't open unless you asked politely, or tickled them in exactly the right place, and doors that weren't really doors at all, but solid walls just pretending. 
It was also very hard to remember where anything was, because it all seemed to move around a lot. 
The people in the portraits kept going to visit each other, and HARRY was sure the coats of armor could walk.
The ghosts didn't help, either. 
It was always a nasty shock when one of them glided suddenly through a door you were trying to open. 
NEARLY HEADLESS NICK was always happy to point new GRYFFINDORS in the right direction, but Peeves the Poltergeist was worth two locked doors and a trick staircase if you met NEARLY HEADLESS NICK when you were late for class. 
###DIALOGUE###NEARLY HEADLESS NICK would drop wastepaper baskets on your head, pull rugs from under your feet, pelt you with bits of chalk, or sneak up behind you, invisible, grab your nose, and screech, ``GOT YOUR CONK!''
Even worse than Peeves, if that was possible, was the caretaker, Argus FILCH. 
HARRY and RON managed to get on the wrong side of HARRY on their very first morning.

FILCH owned a cat called NORRIS , a scrawny, dust-colored creature with bulging, lamp like eyes just like FILCH's. 
NORRIS patrolled the corridors alone.

And then, once you had managed to find them, there were the classes themselves. 
There was a lot more to magic, as HARRY quickly found out, than waving your wand and saying a few funny words.
They had to study the night skies through their telescopes every Wednesday at midnight and learn the names of different stars and the movements of the planets. 
Three times a week they went out to the greenhouses behind the castle to study Herbology, with a dumpy little witch called Professor Sprout, where they learned how to take care of all the strange plants and fungi, and found out what they were used for.
Easily the most boring class was History of Magic, which was the only one taught by a ghost. 
BINNS had been very old indeed when BINNS had fallen asleep in front of the staff room fire and got up next morning to teach, leaving BINNS's body behind BINNS. 
BINNS dRONed on and on while they scribbled down names and dates, and got Emetic the Evil and Uric the Oddball mixed up.
FLITWICK, the Charms teacher, was a tiny little wizard who had to stand on a pile of books to see over his desk. 
At the start of their first class he took the roll call, and when he reached HARRY's name he gave an excited squeak and toppled out of sight.
MCGONAGALL was again different. 
HARRY had been quite right to think MCGONAGALL wasn't a teacher to cross.

###DIALOGUE###``Transfiguration is some of the most complex and dangerous magic you will learn at HOGWARTS,'' MCGONAGALL said. 
###DIALOGUE###``Anyone messing around in my class will leave and not come back. 
###DIALOGUE###You have been warned.''
Then MCGONAGALL changed MCGONAGALL's desk into a pig and back again.

The class everyone had really been looking forward to was Defense Against the Dark Arts, but QUIRRELL's lessons turned out to be a bit of a joke. 
His classroom smelled strongly of garlic, which everyone said was to ward off a vampire he'd met in Romania and was afraid would be coming back to get him one of these days. 
His turban, he told them, had been given to him by an African prince as a thank-you for getting rid of a troublesome zombie, but they weren't sure they believed this story.
For one thing, when SEAMUS asked eagerly to hear how QUIRRELL had fought off the zombie, QUIRRELL went pink and started talking about the weather; for another, they had noticed that a funny smell hung around the turban, and the PERCY twins insisted that it was stuffed full of garlic as well, so that QUIRRELL was protected wherever PERCY went.

Lots of people had come from Muggle families and, like HARRY, hadn't had any idea that they were witches and wizards.

CHAPTER NINE
THE MIDNIGHT DUEL

CHAPTER TEN
HALLOWEEN

CHAPTER ELEVEN
QUIDDITCH
As they entered November, the weather turned very cold. 
The mountains around the school became icy gray and the lake like chilled steel. 
Every morning the ground was covered in frost.

###DIALOGUE###What's that dog guarding?''

CHAPTER TWELVE
THE MIRROR OF ERISED
Christmas was coming. 
One morning in mid-December, HOGWARTS woke to find itself covered in several feet of snow. 
The lake froze solid and the PERCY twins were punished for bewitching several snowballs so that they followed QUIRRELL around, bouncing off the back of PERCY's turban. 
The few owls that managed to battle their way through the stormy sky to deliver mail had to be nursed back to health by HAGRID before they could fly off again.
No one could wait for the holidays to start. 
While the GRYFFINDOR common room and the Great Hall had roaring fires, the drafty corridors had become icy and a bitter wind rattled the windows in the classrooms.
Worst of all were SNAPE's classes down in the dungeons, where their breath rose in a mist before them and they kept as close as possible to their hot cauldRONs.
###DIALOGUE###``I do feel so sorry,'' said MALFOY , one Potions class, ``for all those people who have to stay at HOGWARTS for Christmas because they're not wanted at home.''
MALFOY was looking over at HARRY as HARRY spoke. 
CRABBE and GOYLE chuckled.
HARRY, who was measuring out powdered spine of lionfish, ignored them.
MALFOY had been even more unpleasant than usual since the Quidditch match. 
Disgusted that the SLYTHERINS had lost, MALFOY had tried to get everyone laughing at how a wide-mouthed tree frog would be replacing HARRY as Seeker next. 
Then HARRY'd realized that nobody found this funny, because they were all so impressed at the way HARRY had managed to stay on HARRY's bucking broomstick. 
So MALFOY, jealous and angry, had gone back to taunting HARRY about having no proper family.
It was true that HARRY wasn't going back to Privet Drive for Christmas.
MCGONAGALL had come around the week before, making a list of students who would be staying for the holidays, and HARRY had signed up at once. 
HARRY didn't feel sorry for himself at all; this would probably be the best Christmas HARRY'd ever had. 
RON and RON's brothers were staying, too, because Mr. and MOLLY were going to Romania to visit CHARLIE.
When they left the dungeons at the end of Potions, they found a large fir tree blocking the corridor ahead. 
Two enormous feet sticking out at the bottom and a loud puffing sound told them that HAGRID was behind it.
###DIALOGUE###``Hi, HAGRID, want any help?'' 
RON asked, sticking RON's head through the branches.
###DIALOGUE###``Nah, I'm all right, thanks, RON.''
###DIALOGUE###``Would you mind moving out of the way?'' came MALFOYs cold drawl from behind them. 
###DIALOGUE###``Are you trying to earn some extra money, PERCY? 
###DIALOGUE###Hoping to be gamekeeper yourself when you leave HOGWARTS, I suppose -- that hut of HAGRID's must seem like a palace compared to what your family's used to.''
RON dived at MALFOY just as SNAPE came up the stairs.
###DIALOGUE###``WEASLEY!''
RON let go of the front of MALFOY's robes.
###DIALOGUE###``HOGWARTS was provoked, SNAPE,'' said HAGRID, sticking RON's huge hairy face out from behind the tree. 
###DIALOGUE###``MALFOY was insultin' MALFOY's family.''
###DIALOGUE###``Be that as it may, fighting is against HOGWARTS rules, HAGRID,'' said SNAPE silkily. 
###DIALOGUE###``Five points from GRYFFINDOR, PERCY, and be grateful it isn't more. 
###DIALOGUE###Move along, all of you.''
MALFOY, CRABBE, and GOYLE pushed roughly past the tree, scattering needles everywhere and smirking.
###DIALOGUE###``I'll get PERCY,'' said RON, grinding RON's teeth at MALFOY's back, ``one of these days, I'll get PERCY --''
###DIALOGUE###``I hate them both,'' said HARRY, ``MALFOY and SNAPE.''
###DIALOGUE###``Come on, cheer up, it's nearly Christmas,'' said HAGRID. 
###DIALOGUE###``Tell yeh what, come with me an' see the Great Hall, looks a treat.''
So the three of them followed HAGRID and HARRY's tree off to -the Great Hall, where MCGONAGALL and FLITWICK were busy with the Christmas decorations.
###DIALOGUE###``Ah, HAGRID, the last tree -- put it in the far corner, would you?''
The hall looked spectacular. 
Festoons of holly and mistletoe hung all around the walls, and no less than twelve towering Christmas trees stood around the room, some sparkling with tiny icicles, some glittering with hundreds of candles.
###DIALOGUE###``How many days you got left until yer holidays?'' 
HAGRID asked.
###DIALOGUE###``Just one,'' said HERMIONE. 
###DIALOGUE###``And that reminds me -HARRY, RON, we've got half an hour before lunch, we should be in the library.''
###DIALOGUE###``Oh yeah, you're right,'' said RON, tearing RON's eyes away from FLITWICK, who had golden bubbles blossoming out of RON's wand and was trailing them over the branches of the new tree.
###DIALOGUE###``The library?'' said HAGRID, following them out of the hall. 
###DIALOGUE###``Just before the holidays? 
###DIALOGUE###Bit keen, aren't yeh?''
###DIALOGUE###``Oh, we're not working,'' HARRY told HARRY brightly. 
###DIALOGUE###``Ever since you mentioned FLAMEL we've been trying to find out who FLAMEL is.''
###DIALOGUE###``You what?'' 
HAGRID looked shocked. 
###DIALOGUE###``Listen here -- I've told yeh -- drop it. 
###DIALOGUE###It's nothin' to you what that dog's guardin'.''
###DIALOGUE###``We just want to know who FLAMEL is, that's all,'' said HERMIONE.
###DIALOGUE###``Unless you'd like to tell us and save us the trouble?'' 
HARRY added. 
###DIALOGUE###``We must've been through hundreds of books already and we can't find FLAMEL anywhere -- just give us a hint -- I know I've read FLAMEL's name somewhere.''
###DIALOGUE###``I'm sayin' nothin, said HAGRID flatly.
###DIALOGUE###``Just have to find out for ourselves, then,'' said RON, and they left HAGRID looking disgruntled and hurried off to the library.
They had indeed been searching books for FLAMEL's name ever since HAGRID had let it slip, because how else were they going to find out what SNAPE was trying to steal? 
The trouble was, it was very hard to know where to begin, not knowing what FLAMEL might have done to get himself into a book. 
FLAMEL wasn't in Great Wizards of the Twentieth Century, or Notable Magical Names of Our Time; he was missing, too, from Important Modern Magical Discoveries, and A Study of Recent Developments in Wizardry. 
And then, of course, there was the sheer size of the library; tens of thousands of books; thousands of shelves; hundreds of narrow rows.
HERMIONE took out a list of subjects and titles HERMIONE had decided to search while RON strode off down a row of books and started pulling them off the shelves at random. 
HARRY wandered over to the Restricted Section. 
HARRY had been wondering for a while if FLAMEL wasn't somewhere in there. 
Unfortunately, you needed a specially signed note from one of the teachers to look in any of the restricted books, and FLAMEL knew FLAMEL'd never get one. 
These were the books containing powerful Dark Magic never taught at HOGWARTS, and only read by older students studying advanced Defense Against the Dark Arts.
###DIALOGUE###``What are you looking for, boy?''
###DIALOGUE###``Nothing,'' said HARRY.
Madam Pince the librarian brandished a feather duster at HARRY.
###DIALOGUE###``You'd better get out, then. 
###DIALOGUE###Go on -- out!''
Wishing HARRY'd been a bit quicker at thinking up some story, HARRY left the library. 
HARRY, RON, and HERMIONE had already agreed they'd better not ask Madam Pince where they could find FLAMEL. 
They were sure HERMIONE'd be able to tell them, but they couldn't risk SNAPE hearing what they were up to.
HARRY waited outside in the corridor to see if the other two had found anything, but HARRY wasn't very hopeful. 
They had been looking for two weeks, after A, but as they only had odd moments between lessons it wasn't surprising they'd found nothing. 
What they really needed was a nice long search without Madam Pince breathing down their necks.
Five minutes later, RON and HERMIONE joined RON, shaking their heads.
They went off to lunch.
###DIALOGUE###``You will keep looking while I'm away, won't you?'' said HERMIONE. 
###DIALOGUE###``And send me an owl if you find anything.''
###DIALOGUE###``And you could ask your parents if they know who FLAMEL is,'' said RON.
###DIALOGUE###``It'd be safe to ask them.''
###DIALOGUE###``Very safe, as they're both dentists,'' said HERMIONE.
Once the holidays had started, RON and HARRY were having too good a time to think much about FLAMEL. 
They had the dormitory to themselves and the common room was far emptier than usual, so they were able to get the good armchairs by the fire. 
They sat by the hour eating anything they could spear on a toasting fork -- bread, English muffins, marshmallows -- and plotting ways of getting MALFOY expelled, which were fun to talk about even if they wouldn't work.
RON also started teaching HARRY wizard chess. 
This was exactly like Muggle chess except that the figures were alive, which made it a lot like directing troops in battle. 
RON's set was very old and battered.
Like everything else RON owned, it had once belonged to someone else in RON's family -- in this case, RON's grandfather. 
However, old chessmen weren't a drawback at all. 
RON knew them so well RON never had trouble getting them to do what RON wanted.
HARRY played with chessmen SEAMUS had lent HARRY, and they didn't trust HARRY at all. 
HARRY wasn't a very good player yet and they kept shouting different bits of advice at HARRY, which was confusing. 
###DIALOGUE###``Don't send me there, can't you see FLAMEL's knight? 
###DIALOGUE###Send FLAMEL, we can afford to lose FLAMEL.''

CHAPTER THIRTEEN
NICOLAS FLAMEL
Dumbledore had convinced HARRY not to go looking for the Mirror of Erised again, and for the rest of the Christmas holidays the invisibility cloak stayed folded at the bottom of HARRY's trunk.

CHAPTER FOURTEEN
NORBERT THE NORWEGIAN RIDGEBACK
QUIRRELL, however, must have been braver than they'd thought. 
In the weeks that followed RON did seem to be getting paler and thinner, but it didn't look as though RON'd cracked yet.
Every time they passed the third-floor corridor, HARRY, RON, and HERMIONE would press their ears to the door to check that FLUFFY was still growling inside. 
SNAPE was sweeping about in SNAPE's usual bad temper, which surely meant that the Stone was still safe. 
Whenever HARRY passed QUIRRELL these days HARRY gave HARRY an encouraging sort of smile, and RON had started telling people off for laughing at QUIRRELL's stutter.
HERMIONE, however, had more on HERMIONE's mind than the Sorcerer's Stone. 
HERMIONE had started drawing up study schedules and colorcoding all HERMIONE's notes.

Unfortunately, the teachers seemed to be thinking along the same lines as HERMIONE. 
They piled so much homework on them that the Easter holidays weren't nearly as much fun as the Christmas ones. 
It was hard to relax with HERMIONE next to you reciting the twelve uses of dragon's blood or practicing wand movements. 
Moaning and yawning, HARRY and RON spent most of their free time in the library with HERMIONE, trying to get through all their extra work.
###DIALOGUE###``I'll never remember this,'' RON burst out one afternoon, throwing down RON's quill and looking longingly out of the library window.

The sky was a clear, forget-me-not blue, and there was a feeling in the air of summer coming.
###DIALOGUE###HARRY, who was looking up ``Dittany'' in One Thousand Magical Herbs and Fungi, didn't look up until HARRY heard RON say, ``HAGRID!
